.................................\n\n114\n\nIndex\n\nI15\n\n...................................\n\nINTRODUCTION\n_lis document covers the latest version of the Interactive Software\nInvocation System (ISIS) (12/20/79) discussing the syntax and operation of\nthe Interactive Program Language, IPL.\n\nIPL is based on the higher order\n\n._\n\nlanguage PASCAL and anyone wishing to use ISIS should have a working knowledge\nof PASCAL or have access to a PASCAL Manual (see ref. i).\n\nPASCAL was chosen\n\nas tilebase language because of its simplicity and its wide range of capabilities.\nIPL and PASCAL differences are discussed on page 12.\n\nIPL contains most of\n\nthe arithmetic operations, functions, and control statements of a traditional\nprogramming language.\n\nThis language has been extended to include statements\n\nfor data and text editing, file management, and tool invocation.\nmanipulates pages of text or data.\n\n_e\n\neditor\n\nThe IPL statements allow insertion,\n\ndeletion, replacement, and modification of lines of text or data.\n\nThe file\n\nmanager allows the user to save, access, and purge pages within a 5-1evel\nhierarchical file system.\n\nThe tool invoker allows the user to communicate\n\nwith the host computer system.\nISIS is being developed by Dro Wo Joseph Berman on contract for Langley\nResearch Center (LaRC).\n\nISIS was originally developed under the CDC NOS-BE\n\noperating system at the University of Virginia and is currently running under\nthe CDC NOS 1.3 operating system at LaRC.\n\nThe transportability of ISIS is\n\nbeing tested by efforts to rehost it to an IBM 370 system and to a PDP-11\nmachine.\n\nAnyone having an application for ISIS is welcome to use it with\n\n.i\ni\n\nthe understanding that ISIS is not\n\na production system, but a developing system,\n\nOn the LaRC system, ISIS is stored on a direct access permanent file under\n\n6\n\ni\n\nthe user number 961300N\xc2\xb0\n\nThe control statements to access and execute ISIS are:\n\n..... :_.,::.h_.:..-"L_n:9_!\',\n,::_.t._:i. :\nr.\n,\n_-.\ni.\n:[..,":\'":_Fin\n. ,:,. 0\n..... statements.\n\n- Terminate\n\nISIS session.\n\nINTERACTIVE PROGRA_IING LANGUAGE (IPL) SYNTAX\n\nThe IPL descriptions provided in subsequent sections have the following\nformat:\n\nThe IPL statement syntax at the top of the page.\n\nThe words appearing\n\nin caps must be typed as shown, whereas, the words in small letters can be\nreplaced with appropriate information\xc2\xb0\n\nA discussion of the statement, what\n\nit does, and how to use it is followed by examples illustrating how the\nstatement can be used\xc2\xb0\nThe\n\nSee example page 18.\n\nstatements are discussed in groups according to capabilities.\n\nThe\n\nfirst group, Interactive Programming Statements, contains statements of a\ntraditional programming language.\n\n_le second group, File Management Statements,\n\nallows the user to save, replace, access, and purge information which is\ncontained within a S-level hierarchical file system.\n\n_le third group,\n\nText Editing Statements, contains statements which allows editing (Insertion,\nDeletion, Replacing, and Hodification) of lines of text or data which is\ncontained in the file system.\n\nThe fourth group, Tool Invocation Statements,\n\nallows the user to communicate with the host computer system.\n\nThe fifth,\n\nand last group, Interrogation Statements, allows the user to make inquiries\nof ISIS, relating to statements in any of the above groups.\n\n8\n\nSYNTAX\n\nSyntax Conventions\n\nThese conventions\n\nwill be used in the IPL statements\n\nor in the discussions\n\nof the statements\xe2\x80\xa2\n\n?\n>\n\nISIS prompt\n\n- informs\n\nISIS indication\nyet complete\n\nthe user that ISIS is ready\n\nthat the current\n\nand more\n\ninput\n\nid\n\nOne or more\n\n\xc2\xa3n\n\nLine number\n\nn\xc2\xa3\n\nA specific\n\n[ ]\n\nOptional\n\nI I_\n\nCommand choices are enclosed\nby vertical slashes (I)\n\ncol\n\nColumn number\n\ninc\n\nLine\n\n...\n\nISIS acknowledgement\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nSeparators\n\n,\n\nList separator\n\nis not\n\nIdentifier\n\nid(s)\n\nstatement\n\nis required\n\nJ\n\nidentifiers\n\nnumber\n\nseparated\n\nby commas\n\nof lines\n\ninformation\n\nfor command\nin brackets\n\nincrement\n\nin DATA\n\nto the\n\n_\n\nBASE library\n\nkey\npage name\n\nseparated\n\nBREAK Key\nKey\n\nThe _\nkey has two functions. It enables the user to discard a\nlly typed line and reenter it. This is in:addition to the normal\nkey. It also allows the user to terminate a command. The line to\nbe reentered may be a command statement (statement verb) or a line in the\nACTIVE page the user is in the process of editing. A good example would\nbe if he made a typographical error in the text being inserted. The user\nhits the BREAK key, ISIS acknowledges this by printing 3 dots (...),\nreprompts with the line number for reentry of the line, and then the user\nretypes the information.\nTo terminate commands using the _\nkey, the user simply depresses\nthe _\nkey after he receives the prompt for the next line number.\nNo other information may appear on the line preceeding the\nkey.\n\nEXAMPLES:\n[ FI\'.-;\nERT 4 .. ..-2:\n\n4.\n........\n"\'\n.... \'\n\n=THi S ]::\'.-; M F::.:: P!_\nR\nRt"i E\n\n6,\n=F\'R-_-c,_,_.., _LLi\'.-;TRI"_TIt.ii:@*..,\n.., , .......\n.\n_,.........\nBkL,._RHH IL.LI_I!-;TRFITI_-.iI.:_"HE\n\' "t I\'-\'\n_-_ ......... ...:,E OF THEr..E\',REF_::\n_::B"r!\n\ni_\'_=\n\nI.II::.L.HF..D!HI_\n_11_lht::\n=F:l_IF-:r::...I4,l.i_....\n_:__I,,kBR\n=I::I...IF.\'.r..EI\'] ",\' L::E big "-i" "rFtzli\nIL\n\xc2\xb1\n=(_*\n=F:R\n\ni_:.\n1,::.,\n14.\n\n- Histake here in s___ling.\nUser\ndepressed the _.k_y_..ISIS\n...........\nresponded with 3"tiers and prempted\nthe user for reentry of the line.\n-Another mistake in spelling - User depressed\nterninate\nthe\n\nthe\nBREAK key\ncommand.\n\nto\n\ni _ ,-.= =,T TE:"\n=,:,t"r,qATE_:Io\ni _.-,4 @, \'I. ! \'-:\'\nI... \'.-;\ni T\nYI\'_LI..t\n\n",\n\n4\xc2\xb0\n\n!\n\nL.,!".I\n\n! -_\n.....\n\n=TH!S I\'._; Rt-] E:::.::R[\'iF\'LE\n\n6.\n\n=F:\'F:\'.Oi-_,FItF@I\nILLI_I\'.-\';Tff,:F:!T]:[\'.Ji::_\nTHE\n\':\'\n= ! The KEY\ntype allows the user to define a variable which may be used in the range of\nthe edit commands of ISIS.\n\nKEY values are between 0.0000 and 999.9999.\n\nIn IPL a semicolon (;) placed at the end of a statement is optional\nif it is not followed by another statement on that line.\n\nIf there is more\n\nthan one statement on a line, then the semicolon (;) must be used to separate\nthe two statements.\nIn IPL, each simple statement must be completed on a single line, unless\nexplicitly continued to the next line by having a $ as the last nonblank character on\nthe line.\n\nThe maximum number of characters permitted on a line is limited\n\nto 133 characters.\nAnother IPL/PASCAL difference is in the assignment statement\xc2\xb0\n\nIPL allows\n\neither = or := for assignments, whereas, PASCAL requires a :=o\nAnother difference of IPL is it does not use BEGIN and END\'s to surround\ncompound statements.\n\nAll that is required is an END to terminate a compound\n\nstatement.\n12\n\n\xc2\xb0\n\nIPL/PASCAL\nDIFFERENCES\n\nComments are similar to those of PASCAL in that they begin with a (*;\nhowever, unlike PASCAL, IPL comments are automatically ended with the end of\nthe line.\n\nThis means the user doesn\'t have to close comments.\n\nIt also means\n\nthat comments may not be followed by code nore are they automatically continued\non the next line.\nRecords cannot have CASE variants.\nto be used as part of the variable name.\n\nIPL does not presently allow underscores\nIPL does not allow packing, does not\n\nhave a CASE statement, and does not allow sub range types.\n\n13\n\nSystem Variables Used in Programming Statements\n\nThere are several ISIS system variables which have been made available\nto the user.\nSYSTEM.\n\nThese variables are contained in a record (ref. i, p. 42) named\n\n_le SYSTEH record field identifiers are as follows:\n\nIdentifier\n\nType\n\nDescription\n\n.VERBOSE\n\n-\n\nBOOL\n\n-\n\nIf TRUE, SET, and CLEAR statements print\nacknowledgement. If FALSE, no such acknowledgement\nis printed.\n\n.DELTA\n\n-\n\nKEY\n\n-\n\nThe default range increment {inc) on the Text\nEditing Statement, INSERT (default value is I)\n\n.ALARM\n\n-\n\nINT\n\n-\n\nTwenty-four hour clock alarm - when ALARM\n(clock time) is 0, then a message is printed to\nthe user on the CRT- ***ALARM***. _lis may be\nuseful to a person with a very tight schedule\nand a poor memory.\n\n.CLOCK\n\n-\n\nINT\n\n-\n\nIs the number of elapsed milliseconds in the current\nterminal session (read only variable)\n\n.TIHE\n\n-\n\nSTRING\n\n-\n\nCurrent day time (read only variable)\n\n.DATE\n\n-\n\nSTRING\n\n-\n\nCurrent date (read only variable)\n\n.F\n\n-\n\nKEY\n\n-\n\nThe first line number in a frame.\n\n.L\n\n-\n\nKEY\n\n-\n\nThe last line number in\n\n.C\n\n-\n\nKEY\n\n-\n\n_le current line number in a frame.\n\n.K\n\n-\n\nKEY\n\n-\n\nCurrent line number in a FOREACH loop only,\notherwise it is zero.\n\n.COUNT\n\n-\n\nINT\n\n-\n\nNumber of items in the range of the last\nediting command (other than FOREACH).\n\noUSERNUM\n\n-\n\nSTRING\n\n-\n\nCurrent seven character user number.\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\na frame.\n\nTo obtain the information in this record, the user may inquire with SHOW ID\nSYSTEM, or PRINT SYSTEM.\nnames and types.\n\nThe SIIOWID SYSTEM will print out the field identifier\n\n\'l_ePRINT SYSTEM will print out the current values of these\n\nfield identifiers.\n\n14\n\n_i\n_i\n\nSYSTEM\nVARIABLES\n\nEXAMPLE:\n\ni!.J., \'.\', . _\'::\'\':-\',,FiLFiF.\'.H=:=i,\n4 .-....\ni.q6\n.\n:[i.-.5 4.- ._.i?\n:i:i;\n.:::\'F;il , ":L3F:K\ni"H\'!"\n$9 P.\n\n- Set .ALARMfor\n\n11:56\n\n- Print SYSTEM.CLOCK\n\n\'i ...i, F.1 ,, :i \'::\',\n\'.":\'i F : ":\':\n\nF:\'Fi\'.\ni [JT ,, \'Ti !\'1!!i\n".1.\n\n- Print\n\nSYSTEM.\nTIME\n\nD"3.-""_=\n\n:!,\n1,%5,157\n, L3 ,r.!T TiFi\'l\'!i[\nrz, ,..I\n,\n.....\n\n-\n\nPrint SYSTEM.DATE\n\n?q \xe2\x80\xa2,-_ .._.. .-.\n. ...." _\',:\':\n..., "Z,:.,\n...\nj, , c c- ..::-::,\ni\n,-:,\n\n\'.L:;I.._OH \'.!i!;YSTEH\nI i)\n!"\'."\n\n1" :-:r":l\n\n- Display\n\nSYSTEM\nrecord\n\nr\'"\n\n.-..i ).-.\n\n,...,)....jj\n\n:::\'+=- ..\'" E: i.3\n[\n0 L\n: \'F+;\' ,t ,3 ....\n..... ,. Ei\n2\nPL\np\n\n26\n\\\n\nLOOP\nProgramming\n\nWIIILE\n\nStatements\n\nY"TLE\n\ncondition DO [EXITIF condition]_ END\nstatement(s) _\n\nThe WHILE statement is a type of LOOP statement. The statements contained\nin the loop will be executed WHILE a certain conditions exists. The WHILE\nstatement evaluates a condition, which must reduce to a BOOL result. If the\ncondition is FALSE, the statements are skipped. If the condition is TRUE, the\nstatements are executed and the condition is then re-evaluated. If the condition\nis again TRUE, the statements are re-executed and the condition is then re-evaluated.\nThis process continues until the condition is FALSE. _en this happens, the\nstatements are skipped and execution continues with the next statement.\n\nEXAMPLE:\n\n:!. =2 J.. !.:!::\n;Tii:\n9\n;i.2 =, ii-J. ..\' .....\xe2\x80\xa27 ."............, .", = ,\':: /..i\'._ ....\n; = 7.. :\'\n>:. _;: ".\'r....... \xe2\x80\xa2 .._\n\n12 ,,\'::\'":\'i\' ....... __:\' ,",, _"_\'r::..\n::.=\n..........\n,.\n\' " \'-="""" :\' S=:: . ... k\' bl["i [... The statements contained\nin the loop will be repeated UNTIL a condition occurs. The REPEAT statement\nis similar to the WHILE statement. After setting a tag, all lines of code\nmodified or added will bear the tag-id. This tag-id could be the date\nthe modifications are made, or the name of the person making the modifications. All lines modified will continue to contain this tag-id until\nthe user gets rid of it. The tag may be changed at any time by executing another\nSET TAG command and from there on the new tag-id is appended to the\nmodified code. The CLEAR TAG command clears the tag-id and no more tags\nwill be placed on modified lines of code. After printing the output,PRINT leaves the cursor at its current\nposition, whereas PRINTLN advances the cursor to the beginning of the next\nline.\nThe optional FOPh[AT\nis similar to that of PASCAL in that each\nexpression may have its own format.\nThe format may specify total\nwidth, scaling factorsor base conversions.\nDefault formats are\n\nfield\n\nas follows:\n\nhEAL numbers - an E format type with field width of 22\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\ns\n\nINT numbers\n\n- a field width of I0 with all digits right\n\n_t,.\n\njustified\nSTRING-\n\nBOOL\n\nthe field width is equal to the length\nstring and string is left justified\n- a field width\n\nof I0-and"\n\nright\n\nof the complete\n\njustified\n\nVariables that have been declared but not defined are assigned default values\nb\'ythe ISIS system. Integersand real variables are set equal to zero,\nBooleans are set to FALSE and stringsare of zero lenKth. Discussionof\noptional formats is supplied below. All formats are ignored for ARRAY and RECORD outputs.\nFormat options - :FORMAT1- is the tota! field width. The expressionis\nprinted in the E _ormat for real variables (PRINT x:10,\ny:lb). It can be used with integer, real, and string\nvariables. Where FORMATI is smaller than the number of\ncharactersin a string the field width is ignored and the\ncomplete string is printed\xe2\x80\xa2 If FORMAT is greater than the\nstring length, blanks are added until the string length\nspecified\n\nby the format\n\n:FORHATI:FORMAT2\n\nis printed.\n\n- sets up total\n\nfield width\n\n(FORMATI)\n\n(as describedabove) and defines the number of significant\ndigits to the right of the decimal point. This means\nthe variable is printed in a fixed \xc2\xa3ormat. Thi___.s\nformat\napplies\n\nEXAMPLE:\n\n(see\n\nnext\n\nonly\n\nto real\n\nexpressions.\n\ni\n\n"]\n\nOF !NT\n\n0\'9. Y and Z can be variables, constants,\nor expressions.\n\nINT\nOperators: ,-,DIV,MOD\n+\nFunctions : ABS(x):\n\nAbsolute value of inteser x\n\nLEN(x)\n:\n\nLengthof stringx\n\nORD(x):\n\nOrdinal\n\nROUND(x):\n\nstring x (ORD(\'C\') = 3) [Implementation dependent]\nRounded value of real x \xe2\x80\xa2\n\nnumber\n\nof the first character\n\nof the\n\nSQR(x)\n:\nSquareof integerx\nTRUNC(x): Truncated\nvalueof real x\nLOC(S1,S2):Is $2 a substrlng $1?\nof\nIf $2 is an undefined\nstringvariable(zerolength\nstring)then LOC(SI,S2)\n--i\nIf $2 is not a subs=ring $1 thenLOC(S1,S2) 0\nof\n=\nIf $2 is a subs=ring S1 then LOC(SI,S2) the\nof\n=\ncharacter\nposition(index)\nwi=hin S1 at which\n=he Is= occurrence $2 begins\nof.\n\nREAL\nOperators:+,-,/,*\n\n"\n\nFunctions ABS(x)\n:\n:\nARCTAN(x):\nCOS(x)\n:\nEXP(x):\nLN(x):\nSIN(x):\nSQR(x)\n:\nSQRT(x):\n\nAbsolute\nvalueof real x\nArc-tangent f x radians\no\nCosineof x radians\ne raisedto the powerx\nNaturallogarithm x\nof\nSine of x radlans\nSquareof real x\nSquareroot of rea____l\nor integerx\n\nBOOL\nOpera=ors <,>,<=, <>,=,AND, NOT\n:\n>=,\nOR,\nFunctions:ODD(x): x must be integer. The resultis BOOL\nIf x is odd then ODD(x)= TRUE\nIF x is even then ODD(x)= FALSE\nKEY\nOperators:+,-\n\n39\n\ni\n\nLibrary\n\nStatements\n\nThe ISIS library is a 5-1evel hierarchical\nfile structure.\nThe library\nis where the user save, accesses, and purges pages of information.\nThese\npages of information might be programs, data, control cards, or combinations\nof these. Each page of information is assigned a pagename and is written in\nthe form:\nhbrary,\n\ns,,e _z .book.\n\nchapter,\n\npage\n\n]_\nt\n\nThese levels allow the user to easily describe and identify the information\ncontained on a page.\nEach level of the page name is separated by a dot (.).\nLibrary pages are transferred by page name to frames for editing.\nThe page\nname will remain associated with a frame until the user changes the name\n(SET NAME) or transfers another page into the frame.\nFurther discussion on\nthe association between the library page and the frame is discussed on page 49.\nAll five levels of the page name must be specified if the frame being used\nfor editing has not previously been assigned a page name.\nOtherwise, the page\nname may be specified by typing only those levels of the name that change.\nHowever, when the user changes one level of a page name, then all lower levels,\nif not being changed, must be replaced by the dot separator and a blank space.\nFor example, if the page name is ISIS.CKCASES.SOURCE.PGI.SUB\nand the user\nwishes to change it to ISIS.CKCASE.BINARY.PGI.SUB\nthen he may abbreviate\nas follows:\nBINARY. . (all lower levels must be specified or abbreviated\nwith dot and blank).\nFor the users convenience,\ndefault names have been\nprovided for the first four levels of all new frames.\nThe default names are\nof the forms\nISISLIB.S.B.C.(user\n\nsupplied\n\npage\n\nlevel)\n\nWhere the user only has to assign the page level part of the name.\nBefore\ntrying to store anything in a library, the library file must be created on\nthe host computer.\nThis is done using one of the interface programs, ISISGEN.\nThe interface between the ISIS library environment and the NOS operating\nsystem is handled by 3 utility programs, ISISGEN, ISISPUT, and ISISGET.\nISISGEN\nsets up an NOS file in the format required by ISIS for its library system.\nISISPUT handles the transfer of information\nfrom the NOS system to the ISIS\nlibrary.\nISISGET handles the transfer of ISIS library information to the NOS\nfile system.\nDetailed writeups of these utility programs appear on the next page.\nNOTE:\n\nThe user should try and keep the number\n40 in order to allow ISIS to run fast.\nname is limited to seven characters.\n\nof shelves and books less then\nAlso, each level of the page\n!\n\n4_\n\nJ\n_T\n\n4O\n\nISISGEN\nISISPUT\nISISGET\n\nLI BRARY\n\nSTATEbIENTS\n\nISIS/NOS Interface\n\nISISGEN\nISISGEN is a program which allows the user to create a library for use by\nISIS. A library must be created before any pages may be stored. To do this\nan NOS direct access file must first be created. This file is where the users\nlibrary is saved on the NOS system\xc2\xb0 Then ISISGEN will convert the file to the\nformat required by the ISIS library. The control cards necessary to do this\nare shown below\xc2\xb0\nATTACH,ISISGEN/UN=961300N.\nDEFINE,LIBRARY=isislib/M=W\xc2\xb0\nISISGEN.\nRETURN,LIBRARY,ISISGEN.\n\nISISPUT\nISISPUT is a program which allows the user to take an NOS local\nfile (Nfn) and put it into the ISIS library system\xc2\xb0 The NOS file is rewound\nbefore it is stored\xc2\xb0 The full ISIS page name must be typed\xc2\xb0 This means that\nany NOS file can now be edited by ISISo The control cards for using ISISPUT\nare as follows:\nATTACH,ISISPUT/UN=961300No\nISISPUT,Nfn.\nlibraryoshelfobook.chapteropage\nNOTE:\n\n(see writeup on page 40)\n\nISISPUT uses the smallest possible increment (o001) for the line number\nassignment. This means the user must REKEY the page before he may make\nany editing INSERTS\xc2\xb0\n\nISISGET\n\n-\n\nISISGET is a program which allows the user to get an ISIS library page and\nwrite it into an NOS local file. The NOS file is NOT rewound\nafter it is retrieved\xc2\xb0 The full ISIS page name must be typed\xc2\xb0 Control cards\nnecessary to use ISISGET are shown below.\n\nP\n\nATTACH,ISISGET/UN=961300No\nISISGET,Nfn\xc2\xb0\nlibraryoshelf.bookochapter.page\n\n41\n\n(see writeup on page 40)\n\nLibrary\n\nStatements\n\n[frame-id/] SET NAME [library].[shelf].[book].[chapter].[page]\n\nThe SET NAME statement assigns a library page name to the contents of the ACTIVE\nframe or specified frame.\nThis allows the user to assign a new name or change the\nlibrary page name associated with that frame.\nThe page name contains 5 levels for\nidentification purposes.\nIf the frame has not been previously assigned a page name\n(SET NAME or USE),then each level of the name must be specified (SET NAME library.\nshelf . book . chapter . page).\nOtherwise, the pagename\nmay be abbreviated\nas discussed in the library statement writ=up on the\nprevious page.\nWhen the contents of a frame are saved, they will be saved under the\nlibrary name assigned to it with this statement.\nWhen the user changes the pagename associated with a frame and wishes to avoid\nretyping lower level parts of the name which do not change, he must type the DOT\nseparator followed by a blank to replace the next lower level name.\nSee 2nd, 3rd,\nand 5th examples.\n\nEXAMPLE :\n\nLU.S_i.\n:_;::?Si_T\ni.if:_HhlB, [,i . ,,:.:i ED iFOR ,,PEL:S\ni-IL\nLP.:_ i5.\n_\nS\n- _e\ninitialSET NAME\n........................ :.,., ,::r\',TT!-I ii\'.:=;\n_::_ R. \',"! SAVE places the contents of the ACTIVE frame\ninto the library under the same library name now associated with the ACTIVE\nframe. The SAVE statement followed by an * will replace a page in the\nlibrary of the same name as the ACTIVE frame. At the present time, the user\nmay replace a page (SAVE*) even if the page does not already exist. The user\nshould be cautious in saving or replacing a page to make sure the library page\nname is correct. The page name may be changed using the SET NAME statement\nbefore saving or replacing it.\n\n<\n\nEXAI._LE\n:\n\n\': p; _ :: _i _ : .[I, _: "..\'.;i..\n\n!\n\n_ I!\';;\n\n!!\xe2\x80\xa2:\n\n\'.:1:\n\ni_-,\n\n_-\xe2\x80\xa2i_ ?.- E; EL._ ._\nZ\nN\nEi::.,CH., F:G\n\nC i-I L71\n\nE\n\nL., i..\n\nT_-; _iFi,\'iE :)ff\n\ni- i.J\n\nJ-:_!\n\nW RK\n0\n\n.\n\n...... _ ....... If the specified page\nis the only page in its chapter, the chapter is eliminated from the library.\nIf this chapter is the only chapter in its book, then that book is eliminated\nfrom the library\xe2\x80\xa2 Finally, if the book is the only book in its shelf, then\nthat shelf is eliminated from the library\xe2\x80\xa2 If the page name is incompletely\nspecified, its library, shelf, book, chapter, page parts will be taken from\nthe name currently associated with the ACTIVE frame (or the specified frame).\n\nEXAMPLE:\nII._I.I:::?\'SET"\'-\'" 8L i \'.-\':,[:_::\'.z_NT,\nt.,_Ht!_\nBi-jG,k, CHOP, F\'_.:-:\n,::HOF\'. STATEMENT\nFrame Concept\n\nQ\n\nA working frame is used for temporary storage during editing.\n\nIt may be\n\na copy of a library page which is being modified or may be entered entirely\nby the user.\n\nThere are i0 working frames available to the user.\n\nA default\n\nframe named WORK is provided and 9 other frames which must be named by the\nuser before they can be used.\n\nThe frames are named using the declarative\n\nstatement, FRAME (FRAME WI,W2,W3:STRING;).\n\nThe user can select a page from\n\nthe library, put a copy in a working frame where the code may then be modified\nusing any of the Edit Statement verbs.\n\nThe working frames are also used for\n\ntemporary storage of code for examination or for use with read only statement\nverbs such as LIST, RUN, EXEC, and COUNT.\n\nAny of these working pages may at\n\nany time become the current ACTIVE frame by designating a particular frame\nusing the statement verb, ACTIVE frame.\n\nThe ACTIVE frame does not require\n\nthe frame name as a prefix to the statement verb.\nstatement ACTIVE acts like a pointer.\n\nIn other words, the\n\nIf a frame name is not specified in\n\nthe command, then editing automatically takes place in the ACTIVE page.\ndefault ACTIVE frame is the same as the default working frame, WORK.\nbelow may help explain the frame concept better.\n\nFRA_\n\n.\n\nWI,W2,W3:STRING;\n\n- user declares working frames\n\nACTIVE _ ACTIVE\nframe\npointer _ frame\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\ndefault\nframe\n\nuser defined\nframes\n\n49\n\nThe\n\nThe example\n\nLIST\n\n- list the ACTIVE frame which is WORK\n\nW2/LIST - list the W2 frame (W2 is not ACTIVE and must prefix\nthe LIST statement)\n\no\n\nACTIVE WI - the WI frame is declared to be the new ACTIVE frame\n\nACTIVE\nframe\n\nso now\nLIST\n\n- list ACTIVE frame which is now WI - WI was declared\nthe ACTIVE frame in the above statement.\nWORK/LIST - list the default frame WOP_ (inactive now) by preceding\ncommand with the frame name.\n\nSince the editor must retrieve pages from the library to be modified and\nstore information in the library, an interface between the editor and library\n\n1\n\nis required.\n\nAssociated with each editor frame is the name of a library page\n\ninto which that frame will be SAVEd or from which library information will\nbe retrieved by a USE command.\n\nThis page name is specified and changed by\n\nthe SET NAME or USE statements.\n\nThe specification of this page name via\n\nSET NAME or USE follows the format and abbreviation procedure discussed in\nthe library statement writeup on page\n\nSO\n\n40.\n\nRANGE CONCEPT\n\nTEXT EDITING\nRANGE Concept\n\n"\n\nThe ISIS text editor differs from other editing systems available on the\nCDC Cyber system such as the CDC text editor (EDIT) and the XEDIT system.\n_lese systems are pointer oriented, in that the text to be edited is accessed\nby sliding a pointer up and down the page.\n\nAny line that the pointer is\n\npointing to is the line which is operated on by the editing command.\ncontrast, the ISIS text editor is line oriented\xc2\xb0\nwith respect to the position of a pointer.\n\nIn\n\nIt does not reference text\n\nInstead, the text is referenced\n\nin an "absolute" sense by designating, within each command, the text to be\nmodified.\n\nThis means that each line of text must be capable of being uniquely\n\nidentified\xc2\xb0\ntext.\n\nThe ISIS editor does this by assigning a number to each line of\n\nThe line numbers run in ascending order and represent reference\n\npoints for the specification of the text be accessed by the editing commands.\nThose lines affected by a particular edit command are referred to as the RANGE\nof that command.\nThe use of explicit line numbers, as in the context "from line 1 to\nline S," permit the user to operate on everything within a certain area of\nthe page.\n\nThis range specification is referred to as an explicit range\xc2\xb0\n\nA second means of designating text to beoperated\n\non consists of specifying\n\na search for all lines having a particular characteristic , such as all\nthose containing the string "ABCo"\n\n_lis is the familiar search-for-string\n\nfacility available in most text editors, and will be referred to as an\nimplicit range\xc2\xb0\n\nExplicit and implicit qualifiers can be combined, as\n\nin "all lines containing \'ABC\' between line 1 and:line 5.\'"\nThe explicit range, as mentioned earlier aliows the user to look\nat a certain area of a page, which can be as small as\n\n51\n\none line or as largeas the completepage. Figure 1 showsall of the\npossibilities or the explicitrange. The explicitrangecan consist\nf\nof one line number (\xc2\xa3n). When the range consistsof more than one line,\nthe firstline numberand the last line number to be considered\nare\nseparated a slash (\xc2\xa3nl/\xc2\xa3n2). It is also possibleto put a limit on\nby\nthe totalnumberof lines to be considered\nwithin this particular\narea,\nIn thiscase, the totalnumberof llnesallowedwould appearin parentheses\n\nandfollow heline numbersspecifying\nt\nthe particular\narea (\xc2\xa3nl/\xc2\xa3n2(n\xc2\xa3)).\nThe firstn_ lineswill be operatedon. When the rangeincludesthe\nwhole page the rangewould be specified the word ALL.\nby\n\nAlso available\n\nare multiplerangesseparated commas, This means that more than one\nby\nrangemay appearin an edit statement\nand they do not have to be in _ny\norder, Line numbersused in the explicitrange specificationsre\na\nreferred as KEYS and must be KEYtype variables.Hence,linenumbers(\xc2\xa3n)\nto\ncan be any type of KEY operand, simplenumber,a KEY variable a KEY\na\nor\nexpression.Operators KEY expressionsre addition(+)and subtraction\nin\na\n(-)\nonly. The limitput on the numberof lines(n\xc2\xa3)must be an INT operandsuch\nas a simplenumber,an INTvariable, INT expression,r an INT function.\nan\no\nFollowing\nare someexamples explicit\nof\nrangesused with the different\neditstatements:\nLIST\nKV2\nINSERT I_2=.\n5/KV3/.1(IV3-2)\n0\nREPLACE 2.9,SVI/I0,9/KV3-.\n8(IV2)\nCHANGE \'CH\'to CAT (SVb,\'I\') KV2/KV3-1(2)\nIN\nThe implicit\nrangeallowsthe user to lookat all linescontainiug\neo\nparticular\ncharacteristic,he characteristi.c"\nT\nismade Up -o-fa--s_tr\'_gof\'-_.\n\n......\n\nbe a simple strifig\n\nenclosed\n\nin\'quotes,\n\na STRfNG\n\n52\n\n............\n\nvariableor a STEINGfunction. I\'"I iB:ST:\n.....I"\n\' .\n_\'\'._\n\nI\n\n6O\n\n- LIST a few lines of the\nWI frame.\n\n"\n\nINSERT\n\nText Editing\n\n[frame-id/]\n\n.\n\nINSERT\n\nStatement\n\nrange\n\nThe INSERT statement is used to add new lines to the ACTIVE frame or specified\nframe. INSERT differs from the other edit statements because it adds new lines to\na frame instead of operating on existing lines. Since INSERT is not working with\nan already existing line, an implicit range for INSERT does not make sense.\nThe explicit ranges, ALL_ .F, .L, and .C are not applicable to this command either.\nThe explicit range differs slightly by allowing the user to specify an\nincremental option (inc) separated from the line numbers by a slash (_nl/_n2/inc)o\nThis is the increment ISIS uses when assigning line numbers to the inserted text.\n_le incremental value (inc) must be a key operand (see below). If inc is not\nspecified in the range, then it will assume the current value of the system\nvariable, SYSTEM.DELTA (see page 14). The user is prompted for successive lines\nto fill the range\xc2\xb0 Insertion may be halted by depressing the BREAK key. A\nrange must be specified and may be taken from the table below\xc2\xb0\n\nRange =\n\n_\n\n_\n\nLn _\n\n\'\n\n_---1\n\nn_-\n\nRange with inc:\n\n_\n\n- K[Y o_erand\n\nK[Y expression\n\n_\n\n- INT operand\n\n1n\xc2\xa2 -\n\n.\n\n]\n\n"---_\'--_\n\ni\n\n-\n\nKEY operan<l\n\n- insert lines between and including \xc2\xa3nI and _n2\nincrementing the line number by inc.\n\n_n//inc\n\nNOTE:\n\n\xc2\xa3nl/\xc2\xa3n2/inc\n\n- insert lines beginning with \xc2\xa3n, incrementing the\nline number by inc, until the user halts insertion\nby depressing the BREAK key.\n\nThe user should take care and not insert lines overlapping already existing\nline numbers. An item to be changed (string-idl) and the change (string-|d2)are\noperands.\nThey can be a literal string enclosed in quotes, \'ABC,\' a string\nvariable or a STRING expression. The string to be changed (string-|d) may be\n\nstring\n\nrequired to begin in a specific column (col) or begin between two columns (COll,COl2).\nThe column specification is optional and if used must be enclosed in parenthesis\nfollowing string-id. The column number must be an INT operand. It can be a simple\nnumber, INT variable or an INT expression. TPUT\'+ ), ,\ng\nF\'\nS\nE\nframe.\n\n."\n\xc2\xb0\n\n73\n\n.,\n\nText Editing Statement\n\n[frame-id/] DD\nA\n\nstring-id [AT col] IN range [:[NLINKJNI],[E,IV] ]\n]\n\nThe ADD statement is used to alter existing lines on the ACTIVE frame or specified\nframe. The item to be added must be any type of STRING operand. It can be a simple\nstring enclosed in quotes, a STRING variable, or a STRING function. The string-id\nmay be required to be added AT a particular column (col). This AT col specification is\noptional and if not specified, the string-id will be appended to the end of the line.\nThe column number must be an INT operand such as a simple number, an INT variable,\nan INT expression or an INT function. The range must be included and may consist of\nimplicit and/or explicit ranges discussed on page 55. The altered line contents and\nline number are listed unless a display option has been specified. The display options\nare described below.\n\nDisplay Option:\n\nNL (NO LEST)\n\n- do not display the line number or the\ncontents of the line being added.\n\nNI (NO ITEM)\n\n- do not display the contents, only the\nnumber.\n\nNK (NO KEY)\n\n- do not display the line number (key) oz!y\nthe contents of the line.\n\nEGO\n\n- display the old version of the line, and the\naltered version.\n\nV (VETO)\n\n- user may veto or verify the additionsby responding\nto \'OK?\'with: Y - YES\n- make addition\nN - NO\n- don\'t make addition\nK - KILL - don\'t make addition and\nabort the command.\n\n"\n\n_,,, :fiT\nTM=,,\n_,..\n\nEXAMPLES:\n\ni6.\n@5.i3\'?IJ\'_,E HENVER.\n_LiE:.\nC:KC:A::;E\':;.\nTE?:T.\nPROGRM- Thepageto be edited s read\ni\n16.1 2!"R. [i: !i \':1!\n\n.\xc2\xb0\n\n7S\n\nText Editing\n\nMODIFY\n\nrange\n\nStatement\n\n[:S]\n\nThe MODIFY statementallows the user to make changes in a line of code\nwithout retyping the entire line. Modify displays the line and then asks the\nuser for alterationsto the line with the prompt, "Alters?". The user then types\nin the alterationsusing the followingmodify \xe2\x82\xacomma!}.d\xc2\xa7:_\n\nspace bar\n\n- This\n\nleaves\n\nthe character\n\nunchanged.\n\nB\n\n- B will delete the character appearing directly\nabove it and replace it with a blank space.\n\nD\n\n- D will delete the character appearing directly\nabove it and the rest of the text on the line\nis shifted to the left one character.\n\nI\n\n- I will insert a string of characters before\nthe character that appears directly above it.\nThe characters being inserted must be enclosed\nin quotes and directly follow the I command.\nNOTE that the characters appearing above this\ninserted string cannot now be modified.\nAll\ncommands apply to the character that appear\ndirectly above it.\nThe multiple pass option\ncan be used to solve this problem.\n\nR\n\n- R will replace any number of characters with\na new string beginning with the character\nappearing directly above the R.\nThe string must\nbe enclosed in quotes and follow the R command.\n\nNOTE that the charactersappearing above the\nreplacement string cannot be modified. All\ncommands apply to the characters that appears\ndirectly\n\nabove\n\nit.\n\nThe multiple\n\npass\n\noption\n\ncan be used to solve this problem.\n\nThe range must be specified and may consist of implicit and/or explicit range\ndiscussed on page 51 . Modify providesmultiple prompts to the user for a single\nline, as many times as the user sees necessary to complete the modifications.\nA carriage return\nwith no modifications\npreceding it will discontinue\nprompts for the current line and go onto the next line in the range.\nThe BREAK\nkey will abort the command with no modification made.\nA single modification\noption (:S) is available\nonly one prompt for modifying line.\n\n76\n\nwhich\n\nprovides\n\nthe user with\n\nI\n\ni\nI\n.\n\n,_IOD\nIFY\n\nEXAMPLE:\n\n.........\n! :::. ::;r". 27;\'?USE RL i b3.rlEHYER. This\nfile, referred to as RUN file in ISIS, has the NOS name RFILE. A right\nparenthesis [)] in the first column is used as an EOR mark for separating\nrecords such as the control cards, program source, and data on the RUN (input)\nfile. If control cards are stored on one frame, program source on another,\nand data on still another, the user simply executes the RUN statement three\ntimes in succession. RUN will concatenate the indicated frames to the RUN\n(input) file for each time it is executed. The range is optional and if not\nspecified, will be the entire frame. The line numbers (KEYS) will be stored\nin columns 81-98 if the NK option (described below) is not used.\nDisplay Option:\n\nE\n\n(ECHO)\n\n- Displays the frame contents as it is\nbeing added to the RUN file (RFILE)\n\nNK (NO KEY)\n\n- The line numbers are deleted as the lines\nare transferred to the RUN file.\n\nEXAMPLES:\n\xe2\x80\xa2 \xc2\xb0.\n\n.\n\nFRAME AI,A3:STRING;\n\n- Define\n\nworking\n\nframes\n\n\'\',-\',\n..... $%::-:\'U:\'_-:E :;\'\' .....\nl\'d..\ni:iL. ]\'.:,_ififi\nTE,\n.\n\'"\'",_.Lhi]F.L.L\'-i\'. page from library into ACTIVE\nl;U\'ll.._,.-\'r"\'\n_ Copy\nHL:.6, I :.:: ::... ISIS automatically performs a STORE operation (page 47) to preserve the current\nenvironment and transfers control to the control sequence defined by the RUN\nfile. Upon completion of this sequence, control is returned to ISIS and\nthe current environment is automatically RESTORED (page 48).\n\nEXAMPLE:\nInteractive\n\nUSE\n\nCommands\n\nMYLIBoINTACT.TOOL.CONTROL.CARDS\n\nRUN\nSTOP:SEND\n\nContents of\nMYLIB. INTACT.TOOL.CONTROL.CARDS:\n\xc2\xb0PROC name\nGET,INTERACTIVE TOOL.\nISISGET,INFILE.\nMYLIB. INTACT.TOOL.INPUT.DATA\nINTERACTIVE TOOL,INFILE,OUTFILE.\nREWIND,OUTFTLE.\nISISPUT,OUTFILE.\nMYLIB.INTACT.TOOLoOUTPUT.INFO\nThis control card sequence gets the interactive tool and then calls\nISISGET to retrieve the tool\'s input data from the ISIS library page names\nMYLIB.INTACToTOOL.INPUT.DATA\nand put it on an NOS file named INFILEo\nAfter tool execution (in the interactive mode), ISISPUT is called to\nstore the tools output, OUTFILE, on an ISIS library page named MYLIB. INTACT\xc2\xb0\nTOOL.OUTPUT\xc2\xb0INFOo Completion of the control card sequence returns control\nto ISIS.\n\n9O\n\n"\n\n/.\n\nSTOP:SEND\nStlOT,_N\nFILE\n\nInterrogation Statements\n\nSHOWN FILE\nThe SHOWN file will contain the output of the last SHOW statement which\nwas executed using the KEEP option\xc2\xb0\n\nThe information is saved here for the\n\nuser in case he wishes to refer to it later One\n\nA message is displayed\n\ngiving the total number of lines inserted and the line number of the last\nitem on the file,\n\nEXAMPLE :\n\ni 2 \xe2\x80\xa2 "-\'\' 4_::;\'s\'C:H " "\' ...:,_-.:, U i TL.i E:. R0re:i; l"i \']:.!\';I".i1::1I\'1E Hi\nL\nE Y\nA:!!!; _1"\n.:F\'\nRl:::!\n\'\n0F\n_,\n\n_\n\n%::1 II\n\ni _,\':1. _ \':\' _\':i\n"::\'\n\':;\nI.,.! ."\':_:;\n....ii!_ !\'_0 !.\'.t H !51"_,..\n,_ _:\'\n_\n\n_\n\n_\n\n]:S __\'-_ rlF _.\'\':\'\ni"IE\nIll\n\ni\n\n,,,\n\nI.\',I1_..\n\n102\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\n\',.I\n\nI\n\nSHOW NAME\nSHOW PAGES\nInterrogation Statements\n\nSHOW PAGES\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nI[library].[shelf].[book].[chapter].[page]l\n\n[:KEEP]\n\nThe SHOW PAGES statement is used to display the structure of a complete\nlibrary or a portion of a library. To display a complete library the user\nneed only type the top level of the library name followed by 4 dots separated\nby blanks (SHOW PAGES ALIB ....\n). All pages for all levels of the library\nwill be displayed. If the library name is not included in the statement\n(SHOW PAGES ....\n), it will use the library name of the ACTIVE frame. Also,\nfor the users convenience, this command may be shortened by not typing the\nlast 3 dots (SIIOWPAGES .). This is the only level at which an assumption\nis made. If other level names are not included in the statement, then the library\nis searched for the specific combination of these levels which are specified\nand all combinations are listed. The SHOW PAGES may also be used to search\nfor certain page names\xc2\xb0 For example, to find all page names in a specific\nchapter, the user would type the following: SHOW PAGES LIB.SHL.BK.CHAPTER. o\nTo find all pages named SAM on a particular shelf, the user would type:\nSIIOWPAGE--S--.SHL..SA_4. All books and chapters on that shelf would be searched\no\nfor pages named SAM. The name specified in SHOW PAGES can thus be used to\ndefine an area of search for all pages or for specifically named pages within\na desired region. The KEEP option will store the command output in the\nSHOI_Nfile.\nNote that this command (SHOW PAGES) does not in any way affect the name\nof any frame. This command only displays the names of pages of a library that\nhave previously been saved\xe2\x80\xa2\nEXAMPLE:\n,::.,,:,....._ _._ _.:. hn._,_e (! ]. i b, li_:.,.:,...,e,,,:.i:: .,:l:_.e:i.-\'..es:.i:., F\',"C,\'-._\n, o....... ::=.i:.\n_"\nc\n,,i\ni\nt\'_,::._g - Set library\npage\nF:I ,_: i4EH\':_:\'R F:L::\' F:4E\'$ r ,-_\' T,.....i"# !% \'::"\'!,, :-, [\'HE !.lFi["1 L\'J [,.! Sponsoring Agency Name and Address\n\nNational Aeronautics and Space Administration\nWashington, DC 20546\n15, Supplementary Notes\n\n16. Abstract\n\nThe Interactive\nSoftware Invocation System (ISLS) is an interactive\ndata\nmanagementsystem. ISlS is being developed to provide the user with a powerful\nsystem for developing software in an interactive\nenvironment.\nISlS will protect\nthe user from the idiosyncracies\nof the host computer system by providing a\ncompleterange of capabilities\nincludingdesk top calculator,\ndata and text\neditor,file manager,and tool invoker. The user should have no need for direct\naccess to the host computing system. This documentation covers the operational\nconcepts and syntax of the Interactive\nProgramming Language, IPL, for ISIS.\n\ni\n\ni\n\n17.
